Jamison Brereton

16 (312)
Indra
V─Бmadeva Gautama
21 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This first hymn of the V─Бmadeva Indra cycle is rich in mythological material. It begins with two verses devoted to the journey motifтАФIndra coming to our soma sacrificeтАФbut already in the second half of verse 2 and the first half of verse 3 the legendary poet and sage U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya, who will figure later in the hymn, is intro duced by indirection. The Vala and Vr╠еtra myths are interwoven in the next section of the hymn, verses 3cd through 8, their interpenetration encouraged by the fact that almost no participants are explicitly named in the earlier part of the section. The last two verses clearly separate the two myths: verse 7 by naming Vr╠еtra, verse 8 by the very words of the dog Saram─Б and her naming of IndraтАЩs companions in the Vala myth, the Aс╣Еgirases.
Verses 9тАУ14 concern the saga of the hero Kutsa, the poet U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya, and Indra, a story that is, as usual, narratively elusive. As noted above, U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya was introduced earlier in the hymn by name; he is not named in this section, but deeds involving him in other references to the myth are also found here: Indra and KutsaтАЩs joint journey to his house for help (vs. 10ab; cf., e.g., I.130.9) and the help he provides to their venture (vs. 11), help which elsewhere takes the material form of the mace he presents to Indra (I.121.12, V.34.2).
Our version also has the curious motif of the woman who seeks to tell the dif ference between Indra and Kutsa, who have identical appearance (vs. 10cd). This reminds us of the Jaimin─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa story (JB III.199тАУ200), in which Kutsa was born from IndraтАЩs thigh and therefore looks identical to Indra. Kutsa takes advan tage of this by having sex with IndraтАЩs wife, who claims, when Indra discovers them together, not to be able to tell Indra and Kutsa apart. The Jaimin─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa story appears, at least to us, to have been secondarily generated to explain the enig matic motif in our R╠еgvedic verse, which does not suggest any misbehavior on the part of the truth-distinguishing woman. Certainly Indra and Kutsa in partnership go on to destroy named and nameless enemies and to tear off the wheel of the SunтАЩs chariot (vss. 12тАУ13), an action also prominent, if enigmatic, in other mentions of this story (I.130.9, I.174.5, V.29.10). A successful act of distinguishing Indra (from Kutsa?) seems to be alluded to in verse 14b, bringing closure to this motif. This recognition was aided by the strong light of the sun. It is unclear whether the con tribution of the sunтАЩs light here has anything to do with the damage inflicted on his chariot by Indra and Kutsa.
The remainder of the hymn consists of appeals to Indra for help in contests and battles and for largesse (vss. 15тАУ19), with two closing verses (20тАУ21) summing up the making of the poem and the hopes we have of it.
The hymn is full of deep and surface puns, phonological play, and subtle echoes across verses, and the poet takes some delight in setting up and then frustrating our grammatical and mythological expectations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

рдЛрдЬреАрд╖реАред рдЛрдЬреАрд╖рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛ рд╡рд┐рдЧрддрд╕рд╛рд░рдГ рд╕реЛрдореЛрд╜рднрд┐рдзреАрдпрддреЗ ред рддрджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рддреНрдпрдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдордШрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдзрдирд╡рд╛рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН рдЙрдк рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рдЖ рдпрд╛рддреБ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╣рд░рдпрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН рдЙрдк рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рджреНрд░рд╡рдиреНрддреБ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреБ ред рд╡рдпрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдЗрд╣ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рддрд╕реНрдореИ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╕реБрджрдХреНрд╖рдВ рд╢реЛрднрдирдмрд▓рдореНред рд╕рд╛рд░реЛрдкреЗрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рдЗрддреН рдЗрджрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖реЗрдгреЛрдкрд▓рднреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдореН рдЕрдиреНрдзрдГ рдЕрдиреНрдирд░реВрдкрдВ рд╕реЛрдордВ рд╕реБрд╖реБрдо рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдоред рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рди рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдкрд┐рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрднрд┐рдорддрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдВ рдХрд░рддреЗ рдХрд░реЛрддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the truthful Maghavan the accepter of the spiritless Soma, come to us; may his horses hasten to us; to him we offer this sacrifice, the very potent beverage; may he grant the fulfilment of our desires.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Spiritless soma: с╣Ыj─лс╣гin = from с╣Ыj─лс╣гa, vigata s─Бraс╕е somaс╕е, the Soma of which the essence is gone

Jamison Brereton

Let him drive here (to be) really presentтАФthe bounteous one possessing the silvery drink. Let his fallow bays run to us.
It is just for him that we have pressed the well-skilled stalk. Being
hymned, he will make his meal here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As often, saty├б- тАШrealтАЩ seems here to have the sense тАШreally presentтАЩ, expressing the standard hope of every Vedic ritual, that the gods, esp. Indra, should be physically present at the sacrifice, providing a technical epiphany.

Griffith

IMPETUOUS, true, let Maghavan come hither, and let his Tawny Coursers speed to reach us.
For him have we pressed juice exceeding potent: here, praised with song, let him effect his visit.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHero, Indra, set us free today to give you exhilaration at this sacrifice, as (they let loose a horse) at the end of the road; may the worshipper, like U┼Ыan─Бs, repeat an acceptable prayer to you, the knower (of all things), the destroyer of the asuras.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Unhitch as if at the end of your road, o champion, in order to find exhilaration in this soma-pressing of ours today.

Like U┼Ыan─Б, the ritual adept [=Agni] will recite his solemn speech, his thought, for the lordly one who attends to itтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Rather than interpr. vedh─Б╠Бс╕е as part of the simile (e.g., Witzel Got┼Н тАЬwie die m├╝ndige U┼Ыan─БтАЭ), I take it as referring to Agni, the officiating Hotar-priest, as often. See further support for this identification in the next vs. _________ 03
I take the first hemistich as a continuation of 2cd. Phraseology suggests this connection: the simile u┼Ы├бneva in 2c is matched by the simile beginning 3a kav├нr n├б; together they add up to the full name of the mythic figure U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya. (kav├н- stands in for his patronymic elsewhere: cf. nearby IV.26.1 ah├бс╣Г kav├нr u┼Ы├бn─Б.) The participial phrase vid├бth─Бni s─Б╠Бdhan тАЬbringing the rites to realizationтАЭ has Agni as its subj. elsewhere (e.g., III.1.18 and the other passages adduced by Geldner n. 3a). Agni is also often called a kav├н-, and I take this word here as referring both to U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya to whom Agni is compared and to Agni himself.

The subj. of p─Бda b must be different from that in a; I follow Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) in taking it as the pressing stone. The idiom v├н тИЪp─Б тАШextract/separate by drinkingтАЩ favors this identification; see comm. ad VII.22.4, which passage also contains a form of тИЪarc as here as well as an overt occurrence of the тАШstoneтАЩ (├бdri-).

Unlike Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) I do not take p─Бda c as the main clause with b, nor do I think they have the same subject. Rather with Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra, 48-49) I tentatively take Indra as subj. in c (though not, with Schmidt, a and b as well). The Vala myth is quietly introduced in this second half-vs., with IndraтАЩs creation of the poets and then their singing into existence the ritual patterns. With Geldner (etc.) it is likely that the seven bards are the Aс╣Еgirases.

There may be a very backgrounded pun in cd: c opens with div├б(h) тАШof heavenтАЩ, to be construed with sapt├б k─Бr┼л╠Бn тАЬseven bardsтАЭ at the end of the p─Бda, while d opens with ├бhn─Б тАШby dayтАЩ. Despite the different accent and different case form, it might be possible to take div├б (in sandhi) as a variant of d├нv─Б тАШby dayтАЩ, anticipating the instr. ahn─Б╠Бin the same position in the next p─Бda. But I am very uncertain about this.

Note the responsion of verse-final act. transitive gс╣Ыс╣З├бntaс╕е to vs.-final med.

passive gс╣Ыс╣З─Бс╣З├бс╕е in 1d.

Griffith

Unyoke, as at thy journey’s end, O Hero, to gladden thee today at this libation.
Like Usana, the priest a laud shall utter, a hymn to thee, the Lord Divine, who markest.

Geldner

Spann aus, o Held, wie am Ende des Weges, um dich heute bei diesem Somaopfer von uns zu erg├╢tzen. Der Hotri soll ein Preislied vortragen, ein Meister wie Usanas, ein Gedicht f├╝r dich, den Kenner, den Asurischen.

Grassmann

Ruh aus, o Held, wie an des Weges Ende, dich zu berauschen heut an unserm Tranke, Wie U├зana, so sprach den Spruch der Ordner, das Andachtslied dem himmlischen Beachter.

Elizarenkova

рдХрд╡рд┐рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реА рдирд┐рдгреНрдпрдВ рди ред рдирд┐рдгреНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐рддрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдЧреВрдврдорд░реНрдердорд┐рд╡ рд╡рд┐рджрдерд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реЗрджрдиреАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдЬрд╛рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рд╛рдзрди рд╕рд╛рдзрдпрдиреН рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдпрддреН рдпрджрд╛ рд╕реЗрдХрдВ рд╕реЗрдЪрдиреАрдпрдВ рд╕реЛрдордВ рд╡рд┐рдкрд┐рдкрд╛рдирдГ рдЕрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рдкрд┐рдмрдиреН рдЕрд░реНрдЪрд╛рддреН рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рд░реНрдЪрддрд┐ ред рд╕реЛрдордкрд╛рдиреЗ рд╢реНрд░рджреНрдзрд╛рдВ рдХрд░реЛрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рдЕрдореБрд╖реНрдорд╛рддреН рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рддреН рдЗрддреНрдерд╛ рд╕рддреНрдпрдореЗрд╡ рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╕рдкреНрддрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдиреН рдХрд╛рд░реВрди рд░рд╢реНрдореАрдиреН рдЬреАрдЬрдирддреН рдЕрдЬреАрдЬрдирддреН ред рдЬрдирдпрддрд┐ ред рдЧреГрдгрдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рд░рд╢реНрдордпрдГ рд╡рдпреБрдирд╛ рд╡рдпреБрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрд╣реНрдирд╛ рдЪрд┐рддреН рджрд┐рд╡рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдЪрдХреНрд░реБрдГ рдХреГрддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLike a sage (knowing) what is hidden, and fulfilling sacred rites, so the showerer (of benefits), quaffing copiously the effused (libation), exults (in the draught), and he genitive rates the seven efficient (rays) from heaven, which, being glorified, have made (manifest) the objects of (human) perception by day.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The seven efficient rays: aj─лjanat sapta k─Бr┼лn ahn─Б ciccakrur vayun─Б gс╣Ыс╣Зantaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Bringing the rites to realization like the sage poet [=U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya] a secret, when the bull [=pressing stone] will chant as he drinks out the gush.
In just that way he [=Indra?] begot the seven bards of heaven; just with the (coming of) day they created the ritual patterns as they were singing.

Griffith

When the Bull, quaffing, praises our Iibation, as a sage paying holy rites in secret,
Seven singers here from heaven hath he begotten, who e’en by day have wrought their works while singing.

Geldner

Der die weisen Reden herausbringt wie der Seher ein Geheimnis, er m├╢ge, wenn der Bulle in den Gesang einstimmen wird, den Ergu├Я herausschl├╝rfend, hier die sieben Dichter des Himmels erzeugen. Mit dem Tag selbst haben die Lobs├дnger die regelm├д├Яigen Zeiten gemacht.

Grassmann

Wenn saftdurchtr├дnkt der Held den Safttrunk r├╝hmet, die Opfer f├╢rdernd, wie sein Wort der Dichter, Dann zeugte er des Himmels sieben S├дnger sie machten preisend t├дglich ihr Gewebe.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдХрд╡рд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдирд┐рдгреНрдпрдореН) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддрдореН (рд╡рд┐рджрдерд╛рдирд┐) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕рд╛рдзрдиреН) рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреН (рд╡реГрд╖рд╛) рдмрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрдардГ (рдпрддреН) рдпрдГ (рд╕реЗрдХрдореН) рд╕рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрдирдореН (рд╡рд┐рдкрд┐рдкрд╛рдирдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреН (рдЕрд░реНрдЪрд╛рддреН) рд╕рддреНрдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рддреН (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рдиреН (рдЗрддреНрдерд╛) рдЕрдиреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗрдг (рдЬреАрдЬрдирддреН) рдЬрдирдпрддрд┐ (рд╕рдкреНрдд) (рдХрд╛рд░реВрдиреН) рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рдирдГ (рдЕрд╣реНрдирд╛) рджрд┐рд╡рд╕реЗрди (рдЪрд┐рддреН) (рдЪрдХреНрд░реБрдГ) рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рд╡рдпреБрдирд╛) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдЧреГрдгрдиреНрддрдГ) рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрдд рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢рдиреНрддрдГ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the vast luminous heaven manifested by the rays (of light) is displayed, then are (the deities) resplendent according to (their heavenly) abode; the chief of leaders, (Indra), in his approach has scattered the thick glooms so that men may see.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Indra: S┼лrya, as identical with Indra

Jamison Brereton

When the sun, beautiful to see, was found through their chants [/with its rays], they made shine the great light which is at dawn.
The best of men in his dominance made (it possible) for men to penetrate the blind, bilious shades of darkness with their gaze.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The Vala myth takes full hold in this vs. Instr. arka├нс╕е is a pun, referring not only to the chants of the singers but also to the rays of the sun itself.

The 3rd pl. rurucur has trans./caus. sense here and generally in its other occurrences (see K├╝mmel 431), though not VIII.3.20. In several of those passages itтАЩs in the cadence and would be better read *r┼лrucur (IV.7.1, X.122.5), and here and in the other case (VI.62.2, but not the trans./caus. opt. rurucy─Б╠Бс╕е VI.35.4) a heavy initial syl.

is possible (though not metrically good in VI.62.2). The 3rd sg. act. pf. ruroca (1x: IV.5.15) and act. pf. part. (1x: I.149.3) are intransitive by contrast, as are the medial forms. The anomalous trans. rurucuс╕е forms also have the ending characteristic of the perfect 3rd pl. act., not the -an expected for a redupl. aor. (e.g., (├б)j─лjanan).

Nonetheless I am inclined to believe that these forms originally belonged to a proper redupl. aor. paradigm (├б)r┼лruca-, found in ├бr┼лrucat (3x), with the heavy redupl. proper to a redupl. aor., and that the 3rd pl. forms first adopted the -ur ending of the pf. and then, quite possibly redactionally, shortened the reduplicating vowel. It should be noted, however, that Oldenberg (ZDMG 60: 163) rejects this, an idea originating with Gaedicke.

Because rurucuс╕е is unaccented, the first part of p─Бda b must be the main cl., with the following y├бd introducing a nominal cl. – pace Geldner, who simply declares it an unaccented subordinate cl. verb (n. 4b).

Note the periphrastic caus. vic├бkс╣гe тАж cak─Бra, on which see Zehnder (Periphras. Kausativ, passim, esp. 51). He suggests that it is parallel to the perfect rurucuс╕е in b. If agreement in tense stem is really at issue, this would be another arg.

against my assumption that rurucuс╕е is an old redupl. aor.

The opening of 4c andh─Б╠Бt├бm─Бс╣Гsi is reminiscent of that of 1c t├бsm─Б ├нd ├бndhaс╕е, though they have nothing in common lexically or thematically and they do not seem to demarcate a section. The repetition of с╣Ыj─лс╣г─л╠Бin the next vs. (end of p─Бda a), matching the end of 1a, suggests, however, that some demarcation is happening.

Griffith

When heaven’s fair light by hymns was made apparent (they made great splendour shine at break of morning),
He with his succour, best of Heroes, scattered the blinding darkness so that men saw clearly.

Geldner

Als das sch├╢n zu schauende Himmelslicht durch ihre Zauberges├дnge gefunden war, als sie das gro├Яe Licht am Morgen leuchten lie├Яen, da machte der Mannhafteste das hartn├дckige stockfinstere Dunkel in Hilfsbereitschaft f├╝r die M├дnner zum Durchblicken.

Grassmann

Wenn sch├╢n sich zeigt die Sonne mit den Strahlen und morgens sie das grosse Licht entz├╝nden, Dann macht er hell das blinde tr├╝be Dunkel zum Schaun den M├дnnern, er, der st├дrkste, h├╝lfreich.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬIndra, as the accepter of the stale Soma, sustains infinite greatness, and has filled both heaven and earth by his magnitude; therefore has the vastness of him who has surpassed all the regions, exceeded (the world).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Possessing the silvery drink, Indra increased without limit. He filled both world-halves with his greatness.
Even beyond that did it reachтАФthe greatness of him who surmounted all the worlds.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On с╣Ыj─лс╣г─л╠Бsee immed. preceding comment.

├бmitam must be adverbial, as is recognized by all standard treatments.

I do not see a semantic diff. between the abstracts mahitv├б- and mahim├бn-; what distinguishes them is their metrical shape. The nom. sg. mahim─Б╠Бis obviously excluded from the cadence, but well suited for the break after a 5-syl. opening; instr.

sg. mahitv─Б╠Б- works nicely in a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence. Curiously enough English does not seem to have two different abstract formations to тАШgreatтАЩ (*greatitude, *greatery,

*greathood, etc.) despite the usual flexibility of our language, and so I have tr. both Skt. words with тАШgreatnessтАЩ.

Griffith

Indra, Impetuous One, hath waxed immensely: he with his vastness hath filled earth and heaven.
E’en beyond this his majesty extendeth who hath exceeded all the worlds in greatness.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬKnowing all things profitable for men, ┼Ъakra has, with his willing friends (the Maruts), sent forth the waters, for they, with (loud) shouts, divided the clouds, and, desiring (to fulfil) their office, set open the pasturage of the cows (of the Aс╣Еgirasas).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The able one, knowing all manly (labors), together with his eager companions, gave leave to the waters.
The fire-priests, who split the stone just with their words, opened the pen full of cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

See GeldnerтАЩs long note (6b) on the mixture of Vс╣Ыtra and Vala themes in this vs. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) supplies тАШdeedsтАЩ with n├бry─Бс╣Зi (тАЬMannestatenтАЭ) without indicating what Sanskrit word he is thinking of. It should surely be ├бp─Бс╣Гsi тАШlaborsтАЩ, which regularly shows up with some form of nс╣Ы╠Б- or a derivative thereof (on n├бri ├бp─Бс╣Гsi see comm. ad VIII.96.19). Assuming this is the correct underlying noun, we can identify a buried pun: ap├бс╕е (ap├│ in sandhi) тАШwatersтАЩ opens the 2nd p─Бda; it is phonologically reminiscent of ├бpaс╕е тАШlaborтАЩ.

Griffith

Sakra who knoweth well all human actions hath with his eager Friends let loose the waters.
They with their songs cleft e’en the mountain open and willingly disclosed the stall of cattle.

Geldner

Der M├дchtige, der sich auf alle Mannestaten versteht, hat die Wasser freigemacht mit den anh├дnglichen Freunden. Die Usij, die durch ihre Worte selbst den Fels spalteten, haben den Rinderpferch aufgeschlossen.

Grassmann

Der starke, kundig aller Mannesthaten, liess frei die Wasser mit den Lust-Genossen, Die selbst den Fels erbrachen durch Ges├дnge; den Kuhstall schlossen auf sie voll Begierde.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour protecting thunderbolt has slain Vс╣Ыtra obstructing the (issue of the waters), the conscious earth (co-operating) with you; valiant hero, preserver (of the regions), send down by your strength the waters of the firmament.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You smashed away Vr╠еtra, who had been enclosing the waters. Of one mind with you, Earth helped your mace.
You sped the seaward floods forward, becoming their lord by your power, you daring champion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner tr. p├бr─Бhan as a 3rd sg., continuing the 3rd persons of vs. 6, but the rest of vs. 7 has 2nd ps. reference. The verb ahan, ambiguous between 2nd and 3rd sg., serves as a modulation form, as often (cf. I.32.3d, 4a, for ex.).

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these two vss. tease apart the Vala and Vс╣Ыtra myths that have been intertwined in the previous vss., with the Vс╣Ыtra myth allotted to vs. 7 and the Vala myth to vs. 8. But even with the clear mention of Vс╣Ыtra in 7a and Saram─Б in 8b, there is some ambiguity, centered on the ap├│ beginning 8a. See comm. on vs. 8.

Griffith

He smote away the floods’ obstructer, Vrtra; Earth, conscious, lent her aid to speed thy thunder.
Thou sentest forth the waters of the ocean, as Lord through power and might, O daring Hero.

Geldner

Den Vritra, der die Wasser eingeschlossen hatte, schlug er weg. Die Erde, die im Einverst├дndnis war, unterst├╝tzte deine Keule. Du setztest die zum Meer gehenden Str├╢me in Bewegung, der du durch deine Kraft ihr Herr wurdest, du k├╝hner Held.

Grassmann

Du schlugst den Vritra, der die Wasser einschloss; willf├дhrig half die Erde deinem Blitze; Du triebst empor des Meeres Wasserwogen, o k├╝hner Held, der du mit Kraft gebietest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInvoked of many, when you had divided the cloud for (the escape of) the waters, Saram─Б appeared before you; and you, the bringer of abundant food, have shown us favour, dividing the clouds and glorified by the Aс╣Еgirasas.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When you tore open the rock for the waters, o much-invoked one, Saram─Б had appeared to you before:
тАЬAs our leader, tear out an abundant prize, breaking apart the cowpens, being sung by the Aс╣Еgirases.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just mentioned, verse-initial ap├│ causes some problem. This form matches the two occurrences of ap├│ opening 6b and 7a and grammatically should be, with them, the acc. pl. of ├бp- тАШwater(s)тАЩ. But the problem is that тАШwatersтАЩ do not figure in the Vala myth: it is cows/dawns that are freed from the rock. For this reason Oldenberg suggests reading *├бpo = ├бpa + u, with ├бpa a preverb with d├бrdar, and this conjecture is followed by Geldner However, ├бpa is only marginally attested with тИЪdс╣Ы (only RV VI.17.5 and nowhere else in Skt., at least acdg. to MWms). I therefore accept the transmitted ap├│ and assume 1) syntactically, that тИЪdс╣Ы takes a double obj.

here (тАЬtear open the rock ACC (for) the waters ACCтАЭ), and 2) thematically, that because of the interpenetration of the Vala and Vс╣Ыtra myths just mentioned the cows/dawns in the Vala myth get assimilated to the waters of the Vс╣Ыtra myth. My тАШtore openтАЩ actually assumes that OldenbergтАЩs ├бpa-u is secondarily present, with my тАШopenтАЩ representing *├бpa. It is worth noting that forms of the root тИЪdс╣Ы are fairly rare without preverb. Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 162), Hoffmann (Injunk. 270), and Witzel Got┼Н also all accept the тАШwatersтАЩ reading. Note that the waters here would correspond to the acc. with тИЪdс╣Ы in p─Бda c: v─Б╠Бjam тАШprizeтАЩ. That is, the prize in c is what gets torn out of the rock (waters), while the rock in p─Бda a is what gets torn apart to get to the prize.

Acdg. to Schaeffer (136), the intens. to тИЪdс╣Ы has become lexicalized and no longer has any discernible frequentative value. However, most forms of this intens.

take plural objects, so it could be object-distributive. In our case the pl. ap├бс╕е тАШwatersтАЩ might fit this model, though the pl. tantum тАШwatersтАЩ really functions as a mass noun, not a set of countable hunks of water. See also v├н dardaс╕е in 13d below.

I take adverbial neut. p┼лrvy├бm in b as meaning тАШpreviously, beforeтАЩ, and in conjunction with the injunc. ─Бv├нr bhuvat, as a somewhat awkward attempt to express anteriority: Saram─Б appeared to you previously (b), ordering you to тИЪdс╣Ы (─Б╠Бdarс╣гi, c), and then you did so (d├бrdar, a). Schmidt (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 162) avoids the anteriority reading by tr. тАШzuerstтАЩ, and Hoffmann (Injunk. 270) and Witzel Got┼Н render it тАЬals erstes,тАЭ an interpr.

that would seem to me to require an adj. modifying nom. sg. fem. sar├бm─Б, not an adverbial neut.

Geldner takes the 2nd hemistich as the words of Saram─Б, an interpr. I accept both because of the si-impv. ─Б╠Бdarс╣гi in c and because of the pseudo-anterior construction in b just discussed.

Verse-final gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е has an exact match at the end of vs. 1, and this bit of ring composition signals that this section of the hymn is finished. In the next section we move on to the Kutsa / U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya story.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, these two vss. tease apart the Vala and Vс╣Ыtra myths that have been intertwined in the previous vss., with the Vс╣Ыtra myth allotted to vs. 7 and the Vala myth to vs. 8. But even with the clear mention of Vс╣Ыtra in 7a and Saram─Б in 8b, there is some ambiguity, centered on the ap├│ beginning 8a. See comm. on vs. 8.

Griffith

When, Much-invoked! the water’s rock thou cleftest, Sarama showed herself and went before thee.
Hymned by Angirases, bursting the cowstalls, much strength thou foundest for us as our leader.

Geldner

Als du Vielgerufener den Fels aufsprengtest, da war dir zuvor die Sarama erschienen: “Als unser F├╝hrer sollst du reiche Beute herausschlagen, die Kuhh├╢hlen erbrechend, von den Angiras angerufen.

Grassmann

Als du zerbrachst des Wassers Fels, gepries’ner, ging Sarama voran als deine Botin; Erschliess uns nun als F├╝hrer reiche Labung die St├дll’ erbrechend mit den Angirasen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaghavan, who are honoured by men, you have repaired to the presence of the sage for (the sake of) bestowing (upon him) wealth, and when soliciting (you) in his need (for aid); defending (him) with your protection, the guileful, impious Dasyu has been destroyed in the contest for the spoil.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The sage: the text has kavim, usually rendered as kr─Бnta-dar┼Ыi, the seer of the past; but, here it is a synonym of Kutsa, as in the next verse

Jamison Brereton

In your dominance you came here to the poet in need [=Kutsa?] at the winning of the sun, o bounteous one with your mind on men.
With your help you urged him on at the invocation to heavenly
brilliance; but the Dasyu, possessing magic arts but no sacred
formulation, sank down.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although, as noted ad vs. 3, the word kav├н- often signals a mention of U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya – and this personage figures in the myth being recounted here – in the published

tr. I was tentatively inclined to follow Geldner in taking kav├нm as a reference to Kutsa, since Kutsa could plausibly be qualified as n─Б╠Бdham─Бna- тАШin needтАЩ in this myth and U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya is unlikely to be. However, since the myth in question involves a trip to UKтАЩs place to seek advice (see next vs., 10a), the phrase ├бch─Б kav├нm тАж g─Бс╕е тАЬyou came to the kav├нтАЭ in p─Бda a probably refers to UK, and the n─Б╠Бdham─Бnam, found only at the end of b, may conceal a different goal, namely Kutsa. Hence I would emend the published translation to тАЬyou came to the poet (=UK) (and) to the one in need (=Kutsa) at the winning of the sun.тАЭ In 11d kav├нс╕е also most likely refers to UK.

The phrase nс╣Ыmano тАж abh├нс╣гс╣нau is reminiscent of 4d nс╣Ы╠Бtamo abh├нс╣гtau.

The apparent thematic verbal stem iс╣гaс╣Зa- is almost confined to this group of Indra hymns (in addition to this vs., IV.17.14, 22.10, 23.9, as well as a single outlier I.134.5, for which see comm. ad loc.). NartenтАЩs interpr. of this stem as an aorist generated to the pres. iс╣гaс╣Зy├бti seems reasonable, though it does not account for the limited distribution of our stem: no forms of iс╣гaс╣Зy├б- are even found in the IVth Maс╣Зс╕Нala. (Narten, MSS 1982, cited after Kl. Schr., 266-67; cf. Got┼Н, 1st class, n.

243.) In its other two occurrences (I.129.7, VI.26.8) dyumn├бh┼лti- тАШinvocation to heavenly brillianceтАЩ is a call that we sacrificers make to attract the god(s). I do not understand what it is expressing here. It does not seem to have anything to do with dyumna├нс╕е in 19c below.

Griffith

Come, Maghavan, Friend of Man, to aid the singer imploring thee in battle for the sunlight.
Speed him with help in his irypired invokings: down sink the sorcerer, the prayerless Dasyu.

Geldner

Suche, du mannhaft Gesinnter, hilfsbereit den Kavi auf, der wegen der Sonnengewinnung in N├╢ten ist, du Gabenherr. Eile zu ihm mit deinen Hilfen auf seinen hellen Ruf! Der listenreiche Dasyu, der keine erbaulichen Worte hat, soll erliegen!

Grassmann

Zum S├дnger komm mit H├╝lfe, m├дnnlich starker, der fleht, o reicher, um des Gl├╝cks Erlangung; Gew├дhr ihm H├╝lfe, wenn er dich um Kraft ruft; der zaubervolle, b├╢se Feind versinke.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWith a mind resolved on killing the Dasyu, you came (to his dwelling), and Kutsa was eager for your friendship; now have you two alighted in his, (Indra’s), habitation, and being entirely similar in form the truthful woman has been perplexed (to discriminate between you).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kutsa: a r─Бjaс╣Ыс╣гi, the son of Ruru, also a royal saint; Kutsa is the author of several s┼лktas (RV 1.010), termed as the son of Aс╣Еgiras; there is also a legendary Kutsa, son of Arjuna; truthful woman has been perplexed: after destroying the enemies of Kutsa, Indra conveyed him to his palace, where ┼Ъaci, the wife of Indra, could not tell who her husband was, since both were exactly alike

Jamison Brereton

Drive here to the home (of U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya) with your Dasyu-smashing mind. In companionship with you, Kutsa will become eager.
Do you two, having the same form, sit down each in his own womb. She is trying to distinguish between you twoтАФshe is a woman who distinguishes the truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b bhuv├бt te k├║tsaс╕е sakhy├й n├нk─Бmaс╕е echoes 6b тАж s├бkhibhir n├нk─Бmaiс╕е.

In 6 Indra performs manly deeds тАЬwith his eager companionsтАЭ (either the Maruts of the Vс╣Ыtra myth or the Aс╣Еgirases of the Vala myth); here Kutsa must be transformed into such a sidekick by his association with Indra: тАЬIn companionship with you, Kutsa will become eager.тАЭ On the enigmatic theme of the woman trying to tell Indra and Kutsa apart, see the published introduction. As argued there, it is likely that the Jaimin─лya Br─Бh. version (JB III.199-202), with sexual mischief between Kutsa and IndraтАЩs wife, facilitated by the identical appearance of Indra and Kutsa, is only a secondary attempt to make sense of this tantalizing snippet and no such story underlies our passage. Certainly the woman (n─Б╠Бr─л) in our passage seems entirely upright and eager to distinguish between the two males.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou go with Kutsa in the same chariot, determined to defend him; (you) who are the tormentor (of foes), the lord of horses (of the speech) of the wind; on the same day wherein, yoking (to the car) the straight-going steeds, as if to receive food, the sage (Kutsa) has been enabled to cross over (the sea) of calamity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Seeking help, you drive with Kutsa on the same chariotтАФyou, the goader of the Wind, the master of the two fallow bays,
seeking to hold onto the two silvery (horses of the Wind) like a prize to be secured, so that on that day the poet [=U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya] will exert himself for decisive (help).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although we donтАЩt ordinarily think of Indra as тАШseeking helpтАЩ (avasy├║-) but giving it, in this myth Indra goes to the house of U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya to receive the mace from him. I therefore think that the тАШhelpтАЩ Indra is seeking is concretized as the mace.

See below on p─Бda d.

Note that ─л╠Б┼Ы─Бnaс╕е in b echoes iс╣гaс╣Зo in 9c.

In d the two words ├бhan p─Б╠Бry─Бya have provoked a certain amount of discussion (see Oldenberg, Geldner n. 11d, Kuiper, IIJ 5: 169ff., who is followed by Hoffmann, Injunk. 189 n. 151, and Witzel Got┼Н) because of its similarity to the expression div├н p─Б╠Бrye тАЬon the decisive dayтАЭ (VI.17.14, etc.). The dat. p─Б╠Бry─Бya here is therefore taken by some as a temporal expression with a word for тАШdayтАЩ or the like to be supplied (e.g., Oldenberg p─Б╠Бry─Бya *├бhne). However, the dative expression nearby in IV.25.1 mah├й тАШvase p─Б╠Бry─Бya тАЬfor great, decisive helpтАЭ (though see alternative tr. of Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н]) seems the more compelling comparandum, esp. since Indra has come to UKтАЩs seeking help (avasy├║с╕е 1a). By following ├бhan with the stem p─Б╠Бrya-, the poet may be tricking us into expecting a temporal expression (cf. VI.26.1 p─Б╠Бrye ├бhan; also III.32.14), but the case mismatch should alert the audience that our expection has been thwarted. As indicated in the comm. ad p─Бda a, I think the тАЬdecisive helpтАЭ that UK gives Indra is the mace he fashioned; itтАЩs important to note that in another telling of this myth in I.121.12 the mace itself is called p─Б╠Бrya-: I.121.12cd y├бс╣Г te k─Бvy├б u┼Ы├бn─Б тАж d─Б╠Бt, тАж p─Б╠Бryaс╣Г tatakс╣гa v├бjram тАЬUK fashioned the decisive mace which he gave to you.тАЭ For UK giving Indra the mace, see also V.34.2.

Griffith

Thou comest, fain to succour him, with Kutsa,-a goad that masters both the Wind-God’s horses,
That, holding the brown steeds like spoil for capture, the sage may on the final day be present.

Geldner

Du f├дhrst mit Kutsa auf dem gleichen Wagen als Hilfesuchender, indem du die Rosse des Vata anstachelst, du der Gebieter der Falben, die beiden Schimmelrosse festzuhalten suchend wie die deckenhohe Beute, auf da├Я der Kavi sich f├╝r die entscheidende Stunde am Tage bereit halte.

Grassmann

Zusammen f├дhrst mit Kutsa du begierig, als Stachler du des Windes F├╝chse lenkend, Die rothen haltend, wie erfasste Beute, wenn naht der weise dem Entscheidungstage.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFor Kutsa, you have slain the unhappy ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa and in the forepart of the day, attended by thousands (you have slain) Kuyava with the thunderbolt; you have swiftly destroyed the Dasyus, and you have cut them to pieces in the battle, with the wheel (of the chariot of) the sun.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For Kutsa you laid low insatiable ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa, who brings bad harvest, with his thousands, before the dayтАЩs first meal.
Immediately crush out the Dasyus with (the weapon) that is Kutsa, and then tear off the wheel of the Sun at the moment of encounter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonological play in ┼Ы├║с╣гс╣Зam a┼Ы├║с╣гam тАЬinsatiable ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa.тАЭ With Oldenberg (flg. Geldner, Ved. St.; see also Hoffmann (Injunk. 189) I interpret the hapax kutsy├б- тАШKutsianтАЩ in light of the phrase vadh├бс╣Г k├║tsam (I.175.4) тАЬKutsa (as) deadly weapon.тАЭ The тАЬfuture imperativeтАЭ vс╣Ыhat─Бt in d follows nicely on the normal impv. pr├б mс╣Ыс╣Зa in c.

Griffith

For Kutsa, with thy thousand, thou at day-break didst hurl down greedy Susna, foe of harvest.
Quickly with Kutsa’s friend destroy the Dasyus, and roll the chariot-wheel of Sarya near us.

Geldner

F├╝r Kutsa sollst du den nicht ausdorrenden Susna niederstrecken. Wenn es am Tag auf die Essenszeit zugeht, zerschmettere den Kuyava und zu Tausenden die Dasyu┬┤s an einem Tage in der kutsischen Gewandung; rei├Я bei dem Anprall das Rad der Sonne weg!

Grassmann

F├╝r Kutsa warfst du nieder fr├╝h am Morgen den Fresser ├Зuschna, der die Ernte sch├дdigt; Sogleich mit Kutsa tilge tausend Feinde und rolle vor der Sonne Rad zum Schauen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have subjugated Pipru and the mighty Mс╣Ыgay─Б for the sake of с╣Ъjiс╣гvan, the son of Vidathin, you have slain the fifty thousand Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зas; and, as old age (destroys) life, you have demolished the cities (of ┼Ъambara).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mс╣Ыgay─Б = name of an asura;

Vidathin = a r─Бj─Б; fifty thousand Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зas = r─Бkс╣гasas of a black colour, kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зavarс╣З─Бni r─Бkс╣гas─Бс╣Гsi

Jamison Brereton

You subjugated Pipru Mr╠еgaya, swollen with power, to R╠еji┼Ыvan, the son of Vidathin.
You scattered down the dark fifty thousand. You shredded their
fortresses, like worn-out age a cloakтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the intensive of тИЪdс╣Ы, v├н dardaс╕е, takes a plural obj. p├║raс╕е тАШfortressesтАЩ.

See disc. above ad 8a.

The simile and frame in d are curiously intermingled, with the object in the frame, p├║raс╕е тАШfortressesтАЩ, dropped into the middle of the simile ├бtkaс╣Г n├б тАж jarim─Б╠Б тАЬlike old age a cloak.тАЭ I also donтАЩt quite understand the content of the simile. ItтАЩs presumably the age of the garment, not of its wearer, that causes the garment to fall apart. Witzel Got┼Н seem to take jarim─Б╠Бnot with the simile but the frame: тАЬWie einen Reisemantel spaltet das Alter die Palisaden auseinander.тАЭ This would solve the intermingling problem identified above, but it otherwise doesnтАЩt fit the mythic context. Surely it would be ignominious for Indra if, instead of IndraтАЩs heroically tearing apart these mighty fortresses, they just fell apart from decrepitude and deferred maintenance. The Witzel Got┼Н n. on the passage calls the simile a Sprichwort and it is not clear to me what function they see jarim─Б╠Бas playing.

Griffith

Thou to the son of Vidathin, Rjisvan, gavest up mighty Mrgaya and Pipru.
Thou smotest down the swarthy fifty thousand, and rentest forts as age consumes a garment.

Du unterwarfst den Rijisvan, dem Sohne des Vidathin, den ├╝berm├дchtigen Pipru Mrigaya. F├╝nfzigtausend Schwarze warfst du nieder. Du zerschlissest die Burgen wie das Alter ein Gewand;

Du gabst den Pipru, das gewalt’ge Unthier, dahin dem Sohne Vidathins, Ridschi├зvan; Du warfst zu Boden funfzigtausend Schwarze, zerrissest Burgen so wie m├╝rbe Kleider.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhile having (your) person n in the proximity of the sun, your form becomes redolent of ambrosia, and you are like the deer-like elephant, consuming the strength (of the strong), and are like a terrible lion when wielding your weapons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like the deer-like elephant: mс╣Ыgo na hasti = gaja vi┼Ыeс╣гa; mс╣Ыga iva = a sort of elephant like a deer

Jamison Brereton

Placing your body in nearness to the sun, so that the form of you, the immortal one, could be distinguished,
like a wild elephant, clothing yourself in might, and fearsome like a lion when you bear your weapons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, p─Бda b seems to resolve the problem of distinguishing between Indra and Kutsa that arose in 10cd. The same lexeme v├н тИЪcit тАШdistinguishтАЩ found in 10d recurs here.

The athematic middle participle uс╣г─Бс╣З├б- тАШwearingтАЩ here is a hapax stem and is, of course, morphologically anomalous: the full-grade medial root pres. v├бste is matched by a very well-attested full-grade athem. med. part. v├бs─Бna-. We do not expect a zero-grade formation to this root pres. However, our hapax calls to mind the unnamed hero of this portion of the hymn U┼Ыan─Б (K─Бvya), and the nonce creation of participle uс╣г─Бn├б- here (as an echo of u┼Ы├бn─Б) seems to me a text-book example of morphological aberrancies arising out of contextual pressures – all the more striking because the word u┼Ы├бn─Б does not occur in this section of the hymn (but cf. 2c), so the participial echo is echoing something beneath the surface. Witzel Got┼НтАЩs characterization of this form as тАЬeine individuelle Fehlbildung des DichtersтАЭ itself fails to see the poetic purpose and clever creativity of this form. It is true, however, that it should probably also be evaluated in the context of several other such anomalous participles in this group of Indra hymns, u┼Ы├бm─Бna- (IV.19.4), uс╣г├бm─Бna- (IV.22.2), and u┼Ы─Бn├б- (IV.23.1).

Griffith

What time thou settest near the Sun thy body, thy form, Immortal One, is seen expanding:
Thou a wild elephant with might invested. like a dread lion as thou wieldest weapons.

Geldner

Neben die Sonne dich stellend, da├Я deine, des Unsterblichen, Gestalt in die Augen f├дllt, mit St├дrke dich g├╝rtend wie ein Elefant, wie ein L├╢we furchtbar, wenn du die Waffe tr├дgst.

Grassmann

Den Leib hinsetzend in der Sonne N├дhe, wenn deine Pracht, des ewigen, sich zeigte, In Kraft gekleidet gleich dem Elefanten, die Waffen f├╝hrend wie ein grimmer L├╢we.

Elizarenkova

рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдГ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд╛рджрд┐рднрдпрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡рд╕реВрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рдкрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН рдЕрдЧреНрдордиреН рдЕрдЧрдордиреН рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рее рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗрд╜рд░реНрдереЗ рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛ рд▓реБрдЩреН рее рдХреАрджреГрд╢рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдореАрд│реНрд╣реЗ рди рдпреБрджреНрдзреЗ рдЗрд╡ рд╕рд╡рдиреЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдЪрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдпрд╛рдЪрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╡рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдирдХрд╛рдорд╛рдГ рдЙрдХреНрдереИрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реИрдГ рд╢рд╢рдорд╛рдирд╛рд╕рдГ рд╢рдВрд╕рдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ ред рддрджрд╛ рд╕реЛрд╜рдпрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдУрдХреЛ рди рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдорд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕ рдЗрд╡ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рд░рдгреНрд╡рд╛ рд░рдордгреАрдпрд╛ рд╕реБрджреГрд╢реАрд╡ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдореАрд░рд┐рд╡ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее рее резреп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRelying (upon Indra) for protection, and desirous of riches, (pious men) repair to him soliciting his presence in the sacrifice, as if in the battle, asking for food, celebrating his praise with hymns, for he is the refuge (of his worshippers), and resembles the grateful and lovely (goddess) of nutrition.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I.e. goddess Lakс╣гm─л

Jamison Brereton

To Indra have desires gone seeking goods, taking their pleasure at the soma-pressing as if at a (contest) having the sun as its prize,
(desires) seeking fame, laboring with hymns, delightful like a home, like prosperity beautiful to see.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The simile in b, sv├аrm─лс╕╖he n├б тАЬas if at (a contest) with the sun as its prize,тАЭ provides a transition from the sun-winning myth of Indra and Kutsa, which occupied the previous few vss., and this more general final section of the hymn.

The desires (k─Б╠Бm─Бс╕е) that are the grammatical subject of this vs. – namely our desires for IndraтАЩs largesse – take part in actions that might appear to be more appropriate to other subjects. On the one hand, they тАЬtake pleasure in the pressingтАЭ (s├бvane cak─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е); we would rather expect the god Indra to do so. On the other, they тАЬperform ritual labor with hymnsтАЭ (┼Ыa┼Ыam─Бn─Б╠Бsa uktha├нс╕е), a priestly activity. The desires thus mediate between the two poles of ritual participation.

Pace Oldenberg, ├│kaс╕е in d is most likely not an acc. goal to be construed with agman in a (though this might be a possible secondary reading), but a nominative – on the basis of a web of formulaic associations with raс╣Зv├б- тАШdelightfulтАЩ. Cf. I.66.3 ├│ko n├б raс╣Зv├бс╕е тАЬ(Agni) delightful like a homeтАЭ; also I.69.4-5 raс╣Зv├│ duroс╣З├й тАЬa joy in the house,тАЭ X.64.11 [=I.144.7] raс╣Зv├бс╕е тАж iva kс╣г├бyaс╕е тАЬdelightful тАж like a dwelling,тАЭ X.33.6 kс╣г├йtraс╣Г n├б raс╣Зv├бm тАЬdelightful like a dwelling place.тАЭ The problem in our passage is that raс╣Зv─Б╠Б(the only possible underlying form given its sandhi context) cannot technically modify neut. ├│kaс╕е, despite the formulaics just discussed. The solution, as Geldner saw (n. 15d), is that nom. sg. fem. raс╣Зv─Б╠Бalso participates in the second simile in this p─Бda, sudс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─лva puс╣гс╣н├нс╕е тАЬlike prosperity beautiful to seeтАЭ – with which raс╣Зv├б- also has formulaic associations. Cf. I.65.5 puс╣гс╣н├нr n├б raс╣Зv─Б╠БтАЬlike thriving that brings delightтАЭ (immediately followed by kс╣гit├нс╕е тАШdwelling placeтАЩ) and II.4.4 raс╣Зv─Б╠БтАж iva puс╣гс╣н├нс╕е тАШid.тАЩ. Of course, both similes provide comparisons to the desires that are the ultimate subject, with raс╣Зv─Б╠Бas the pivotal tert. comp. in both – though it does not match k─Б╠Бm─Бс╕е in gender or number.

Griffith

Wishes for wealth have gone to Indra, longing for him in war for light and at libation,
Eager for glory, labouring with praisesongs: he is like home, like sweet and fair nutrition.

Geldner

Zu Indra sind Gutes verlangend die W├╝nsche gekommen, an der Somaspende wie an der Schlacht ihre Freude habend, Ruhm suchend, diensteifrig mit Preisliedern, erfreulich wie das Heim, wie der sch├╢n zu schauende Wohlstand.

Grassmann

Zu Indra kamen W├╝nschende begehrend, das Opfer liebend wie des Gl├╝cks Erlangung, Nach Gut verlangend, sich mit Spr├╝chen m├╝hend, wie liebe Heimat, wie willkommne Nahrung.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet us invoke that gracious Indra who has made so many things good for man; who, bestowing enviable opulence, quickly brings acceptable food to a worshipper like me.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just him, Indra easy to call, would we call upon for youтАФhim who performed the many manly (labors),
who quickly brings a prize worth securing even to a singer like me, him whose largesse is eagerly sought.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take cid with the dat. m─Б╠Бvate jaritr├й since I do not see how to construe it sensibly with g├бdhyam. I cannot explain its displacement to p─Бda end, however.

On the g├бdhyaс╣Г v─Б╠Бjam see 11c.

Griffith

Call we for you that Indra, prompt to listen, him who hath done so much for men’s advantage;
Who, Lord of envied bounty, to a singer like me brings quickly booty worth the capture.

Geldner

Diesen Indra, der sich gern rufen l├д├Яt, wollen wir f├╝r euch rufen, der diese vielen Mannestaten getan hat, der einem S├дnger gleich mir alsbald sogar deckenhohen Gewinn einbringt, der beneidenswerte Belohnungen hat.

Grassmann

Lasst Indra rufen uns, der gern erh├╢ret, der diese vielen Heldenthaten wirkte, Erw├╝nschtes Gut besitzend, solchem S├дnger, wie ich bin, eilend reiche Beute zuf├╝hrt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬHero, indra, when in any conflict of men the sharp thunderbolt falls in the midst (of them), and when, lord there is a terrible battle, then the defender of our person ns is made known.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If a sharp missile will fly in an instant amid some one of the peoples, o champion,
if there will be a terrible clash, o comrade, then, as ever, become the herdsmen of our body.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda b is difficult. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) construe the two locatives in b, k├бsmi├▒ cid and muhuk├й, together, which would of course be the default interpr. However, this leads Geldner to render muhuk├б- as тАШSchlachtgeschreiтАЩ, a tr. for which there is no support: its closest etymological relative, adverbial m├║hur, only means тАШsuddenly, in an instantтАЩ. (Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬin irgendeinem pl├╢tzlichen VorfallтАЭ at least imposes less content and sticks closer semantically to m├║hur and company.) In the published translation I separate the two locatives, taking muhuk├й as a simple temporal and construing the indefinite k├бsmi├▒ cid with the gen. pl. j├бn─Бn─Бm. This interpr. was in part prompted by the need to have something for ant├бr to govern: ant├бr does not take the genitive, so a direct connection with j├бn─Бn─Бm (тАЬamong the peoplesтАЭ) is out, but it regularly takes the locative. Hence my тАЬamong some one of the peoplesтАЭ: since j├бna- can refer to a group of persons who make up a people, it doesn’t have to be a single individual, hence my тАЬsome oneтАЭ rather than тАЬsomeone.тАЭ (Cf. also V.74.2 k├бsmin тАж j├бne.) However, I recognize that this interpr. is both artificial and awkward, and (somewhat in the spirit of Witzel Got┼Н) I have cast about for an interpr. of muhuk├й, which should literally mean тАШinstantaneousтАЩ, that both reflects its etymology and yet allows it to refer to a conflict and be plausibly construed with j├бn─Бn─Бm. The Engl. word тАШskirmishтАЩ (тАЬan episode of irregular or unpremeditated conflictтАЭ) comes close. I would thus revise my tr. of ab to тАЬIf a sharp missile will fly within some sudden skirmish of the peoples, o champion, …тАЭ

Griffith

When the sharp-pointed arrow, O thou Hero, flieth mid any conflict of the people,
When, Faithful One, the dread encounter cometh, then be thou the Protector of our body.

Geldner

Grassmann

Will you be the helper of V─БmadevaтАЩs insights? Will you be a partnerтАФ no wolfтАФat the winning of prizes?
We have come after you (who are) solicitude for us. Widely proclaimed, may you always be there for the singer.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The morphological ambiguity of bh├║vaс╕е (injunctive or subjunctive) allows for several possible interpretations of the first half-vs. Geldner takes bh├║vaс╕е as imperatival тАЬsei,тАЭ though this is unlikely given the morphology. Hoffmann (Injunk.

  1. takes it as a тАЬgenerell oder resulativ konstatierendтАЭ injunctive and tr. тАЬdu bistтАЭ (so also Witzel Got┼Н). By contrast, I think these two fronted bh├║vaс╕е are subjunctives and questions. There is of course no way to tell. However, the purpose clause with subjunctive in 20cd .. y├бth─Б тАж ├бsan naс╕е … avit─Б тАЬso that he will be our helper,тАЭ matching our p─Бda a bh├║vo тАШvit─Б╠Б, suggests that bh├║vaс╕е is indeed a subjunctive and that further we are not at this point certain that Indra will become what we want him to – hence a question rather that a statement is more appropriate. As for how bh├║vas,

-at came to be aor. injunctives homonymous with the morphologically more transparent root aor. subjunctives, I find HoffmannтАЩs scenario (56) plausible, that they were secondarily generated to 1st sg. bhuvam (e.g., X.48.1; 49.1, 4; 86.5), which is the properly built injunctive to the root aor. (though cf. TS II.5.1.1 bh┼лvam). However, I do not follow Hoffmann in taking the motivation for this formation the avoidance of monosyllabic forms, since injunc. bh┼л╠Бs, bh┼л╠Бt are quite common. (A more likely explan. in the Hoffmannian mode would be that, since bh┼л╠Бs, bh┼л╠Бt can do double duty as imperative substitutes, bhuvas, -at make the injunctive value clearer.) IтАЩd rather suggest a different reason why injunctive bh├║vas, -at took hold and could exist simultaneously with the subjunctives of the same shape, while putative injunctives k├бras, -at, secondarily built in the same way as bh├║vas, -at to 1st sg. karam, are essentially only subjunctives. Because of the lack of ablaut of тИЪbh┼л, the zero-grade of the root syllable of the subjunctive bh├║vas, -at doesnтАЩt accord with standard subjunctive formations and must have seemed at best equivocal, whereas k├бras, -at is a perfect specimen of a subjunctive and does not invite other morphological interpretations.

English translation:

тАЬIn every battle, Maghavan, may we, along with those men who trust in you and offer rich gifts, like those who are resplendent with riches, triumphing over their foes, glorify you many nights and years.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

While we dominate the strangers in every contest with these men who seek you, Indra, with the bounteous ones, o bounteous one,
just as the heavens dominate with their heavenly brilliance, may we find elation through many nights and autumns.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. supply a verb in ab: Geldner тАЬrufe ich,тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н тАЬbitten тАж wir.тАЭ This seems unnecessary: the instr. phrases in ab can be parallel to dyumna├нс╕е in the simile in c, all controlled by the participial phrase abh├н s├бntaс╕е тАЬ(we) dominatingтАЭ in c.

One of the factors that might support supplying a verb in ab is the otherwise apparently orphaned acc. encl. tv─Б at the end of p─Бda a, but even as Geldner advances this reason for supplying a verb (n. 19a), he also suggests that tv─Б could be dependent on immediately preceding tv─Бy├║bhiс╕е, an explanation that the close sandhi of the two words (tv─Бy├║bhiс╣г с╣нv─Б) might favor.

In b v├н┼Ыve, in the phrase v├н┼Ыva ─Бja├║, must be a loc., although we might expect the pronominal form v├н┼Ыvasmin. It is, however, worth noting that v├н┼Ыvasmin is found only twice in the RV, in the same phrase (v├н┼Ыvasmin bh├бre) in adjacent hymns in the Xth Maс╣Зс╕Нala (X.49.1, X.50.4). A nominal-type loc. v├н┼Ыve here would also be facilitated by the plural version v├н┼Ыveс╣гu … ─Бj├нс╣гu in I.130.8 with simple truncation of the -с╣гu.

Although Geldner construes dyumna├нс╕е not in the simile but as an attribute of the subject (тАЬweтАЭ), the almost identical X.115.7 dy─Б╠Бvo n├б dyumna├нr abh├н s├бnti m─Б╠Бnuс╣г─Бn may (but need not) support keeping it with the simile; Geldner separates the two in his tr.

of that passage as well.

Griffith

O Indra, with these men who love thee truly, free givers, Maghavan, in every battle,
May we rejoice through many autumns, quelling our foes, as days subdue the nights with splendour.

Geldner

Mit diesen dir ergebenen M├дnnern, o Indra, mit den freigebigen, du Freigebiger, rufe ich dich in jedem Kampfe. Die Nebenbuhler an Glanz ├╝berragend wie der Himmel die Erde, m├╢chten wir viele N├дchte und Herbste schwelgen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTherefore we offer to the vigorous Indra, the showerer (of benefits), holy adoration, that he may never withdraw his friendly (actions) from us, and that he may be our powerful protector, the defender of (our) person ns, as the Bhс╣Ыgus (fabricate) a car (for use).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bhс╣Ыgavo na ratham: bhс╣Ыgavo = d─лptas takс╣г─Бс╣Зaс╕е, bright or dexterous carpenters; i.e. as a wheelwright makes a chariot for a special purpose, so the worshipper performs worship in order to secure Indra’s favour

Jamison Brereton

Just in this way we have made a sacred formulation for Indra, the bull-strong bull, as the Bhr╠еgus do a chariot,
so that he will never keep us far away from his partnership, and he will be our powerful helper, the protector of our bodies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. (Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н]) take viy├│с╣гat as intransitive, a view argued for by Narten (Sig. aor. 214), with a neut. pl. subj. (sakhy─Б╠Б) of a sg. verb. For my argument for a trans. interpr. of this s-aorist, see comm. ad II.32.2. As at II.32.2 I take sakhy─Б╠Бhere as an instr. sg. of separation, though an acc. pl. obj. (тАЬhe will not keep our partnerships far awayтАЭ) is also possible.

Note that tan┼лp─Б╠Бс╕е picks up 7d tanv├▓ bodhi gop─Б╠Бс╕е.

20-21 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. provide a double ending to this hymn. The first (20) begins, as summary vss. often do, with ev├б тАШjust in this wayтАЩ. It announces selfreferentially, with the root aor. akarma тАЬwe have just made,тАЭ that the hymn being completed is the br├бhman- we have created for Indra. And, as noted above ad vs. 18, the purpose clauses with subjunctive provide reassurance for the worried questions in 18ab. Vs. 21 is repeated as the final verse of the seven hymns IV.17, 19-24, so it serves as a refrain vs. for (some of) the V─Бmadeva Indra hymns. It also announces, with a root aor. (though aor. passive), that the formulation has just been made (├бk─Бri тАж br├бhma). Despite the apparent duplication, we should not necessarily assume that this refrain was tacked onto an already complete hymn, because gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е at the end of 21a may form a ring with the same word at the end of vs. 1.

Griffith

Now, as the Bhrgus wrought a car, for Indra the Strong, the Mighty, we our prayer have fashioned,
That he may, ne’er withdraw from us his friendship, but be our bodies’ guard and strong defender.

Geldner

So haben wir dem Indra, dem m├дnnlichen Bullen, eine Erbauung gemacht, wie die Bhrigu┬┤s einen Wagen, auf da├Я sich niemals unsere Freundschaft l├╢se und uns ein m├дchtiger G├╢nner und Leibessch├╝tzer sei.

Grassmann

So haben wir dem starken Stiere, Indra, Gebet gemacht wie Bhrigu’s einst den Wagen, Dass unsre Freundschaft nimmer er verschm├дhe und sei ein starker Sch├╝tzer unsrer Leiber.

English translation:

тАЬGlorified (in the past), glorified, Indra, at present, satisfy your worshipper with food, as rivers (are filled with water); lord of horses, a new hymn has been made for you; may we possessed of chariots, be ever delighted in (your) praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАУ Now praised, o Indra, now being sung, make refreshment swell for the singer like rivers.

always win.

The standard tr. (Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н]) as also K├╝mmel (300) interpr. p─лpeс╕е as hortative.

This is certainly possible (and is reflected in the published translation), but context would also allow тАЬyou (have) made swellтАЭ or тАЬyou make swellтАЭ just as easily.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. provide a double ending to this hymn. The first (20) begins, as summary vss. often do, with ev├б тАШjust in this wayтАЩ. It announces selfreferentially, with the root aor. akarma тАЬwe have just made,тАЭ that the hymn being completed is the br├бhman- we have created for Indra. And, as noted above ad vs. 18, the purpose clauses with subjunctive provide reassurance for the worried questions in 18ab. Vs. 21 is repeated as the final verse of the seven hymns IV.17, 19-24, so it serves as a refrain vs. for (some of) the V─Бmadeva Indra hymns. It also announces, with a root aor. (though aor. passive), that the formulation has just been made (├бk─Бri тАж br├бhma). Despite the apparent duplication, we should not necessarily assume that this refrain was tacked onto an already complete hymn, because gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е at the end of 21a may form a ring with the same word at the end of vs. 1.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдиреБ) рд╕рджреНрдпрдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдЛрдЪрд┐ рддреБрдиреБрдШреЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред (рд╕реНрддреБрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) (рдиреБ) (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреН (рдЗрд╖рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рджреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдореН (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХрд╛рдп (рдирджреНрдпрдГ) (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдкреАрдкреЗрдГ) рдкреНрдпрд╛рдпрдп (рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╣рд░рд┐рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рд╜рд╢реНрд╡рдГ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рдЕрд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдпрдВ рдзрдирдореН (рдирд╡реНрдпрдореН) рдирд╡реАрдирдореН (рдзрд┐рдпрд╛) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рд░рдереНрдпрдГ) рд░рдереЗрд╖реБ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдГ (рд╕рджрд╛рд╕рд╛рдГ) рджрд╛рд╕реИрдГ рд╕реЗрд╡рдХреИрд╕реНрд╕рд╣ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ реереирезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдпреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдГ рдкрд░реАрдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддреЛ рдирджреАрд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рддрд░реНрдкреНрдкрдХреЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡ рдЗрд╡ рд╕реБрдЦреЗрди рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдЧрдордпрд┐рддрд╛ рднрд╡реЗрддреН рддрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдзреАрд╢рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рддрджрд╛рд╜рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╕рддрддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрд┐рдиреЛ рднрд╡реЗрдореЗрддрд┐ реереирезрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рд╜рдорд╛рддреНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реереирезрее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреЛ рдорд╛рдгреВрд╕ рдкрд░реАрдХреНрд╖рдХ, рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдп рд╡ рдирджреАрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪрд╛ рддреГрдкреНрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрддрд╛, рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рд╕реБрдЦрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рджреБрд╕рд▒реНрдпрд╛ рдард┐рдХрд╛рдгреА рдкреЛрдЪрд╡рд┐рдгрд╛рд░рд╛ рдЕрд╕реЗрд▓ рддрд░ рддреНрдпрд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдзреАрд╢ рдХрд░реВрди рдиреЛрдХрд░рд╛рдВрд╕рд╣ рдЖрдореНрд╣реА рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдЖрдЬреНрдЮреЗрдиреБрд╕рд╛рд░ рд╡рд░реНрддрди рдХрд░реВрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдиреА рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее реирез рее
